## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position, velocity, and time. The acceleration in such systems typically involves restoring forces (functions of x), damping terms (functions of v), and possibly driving forces (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Cubic nonlinearity (Duffing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (Duffing oscillator restoring force)
- Linear damping + restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (damped harmonic oscillator)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (damped Duffing oscillator)
- Van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (Van der Pol oscillator with nonlinear damping)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (forced damped oscillator)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Cubic + quintic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order Duffing)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (nonlinear pendulum restoring force)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)
- Mathieu-type parametric: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (parametrically driven oscillator)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v (mixed nonlinear coupling)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven Duffing oscillator)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring force → odd-power polynomial in x (x, x**3, x**5) to maintain symmetry of potential well
- Nonlinear damping → velocity terms with odd powers (v, v**3) or position-dependent damping (x**2 * v)
- Self-sustained oscillations → negative linear damping combined with positive nonlinear damping: (c0 - c1*x**2)*v
- Periodic external driving → sinusoidal functions of time: sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) as additive forcing terms
- Softening/hardening spring → sign of cubic coefficient x**3 determines whether resonance frequency decreases or increases with amplitude
- Parametric excitation → time-dependent coefficient multiplying position: f(t)*x indicates parametric resonance
- Conservative system test → if dv_dt depends only on x (no v or t terms), the system is energy-conserving
- Symmetry breaking → even powers of x (x**2) indicate asymmetric potential wells

Let me simplify the GT:
- `-1.29395390256765*x*(0.0943056786339846*|v|^(1/3) + 1)` expands to `-1.29395390256765*x - 1.29395390256765*0.0943056786339846*x*|v|^(1/3)` = `-1.29395390256765*x - 0.122025...*x*|v|^(1/3)`
- Combined with the other `-1.29395390256765*x`: total x term is `-2.5879...*x`

So GT = `-2.5879...*x - 1.2940...*x³ - 0.1220...*x*|v|^(1/3) - 0.8961...*v - 0.4481...*sin(v)`

The GT has these basis functions:

- **`x*|v|^(1/3)`** term - very few candidates will have this
- **`sin(v)`** term - only a few candidates have sin(v)

None of the candidates contain `|v|^(1/3)` or `Abs(v)**0.333` terms. The GT requires this specific nonlinear term. Let me verify there's no way to construct it from the available terms in any candidate.

Going through all candidates systematically, none contain `|v|^(1/3)` or any fractional power of `|v|`. The candidates use combinations of:
- Polynomials in x and v
- sin/cos of various arguments
- log/exp combinations
- Powers of (c+t), (c+x), (c+v)

The term `x*|v|^(1/3)` cannot be exactly represented by any of these. Even candidates with `(c+v)**c` like Candidate 39, 43, 45, 113 have `v*(c4+x)^c6` or `x*(c4+v)^c5` type terms, but `x*(c+v)^c` is NOT the same as `x*|v|^(1/3)` because `(c+v)^(1/3)` ≠ `|v|^(1/3)` for any constant c (unless c=0, but then it's `v^(1/3)` not `|v|^(1/3)`, and these differ for negative v).

Since v takes both positive and negative values, `|v|^(1/3)` is fundamentally different from `v^(1/3)` (which involves complex numbers for negative v in standard math). No candidate can reproduce this.

Therefore, **no candidate matches the GT**.
